  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_3332617565" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3332617565" />
    <a title="Bee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74099824-bee"><img alt="Bee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604783922p2/74099824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3332617565?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bee" href="/user/show/74099824-bee">Bee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/74099824-bee?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/74099824-bee?shelf=badly-written">badly-written</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/74099824-bee?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/74099824-bee?shelf=anti-hero">anti-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/74099824-bee?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/74099824-bee?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/74099824-bee?shelf=hot-hot-hot">hot-hot-hot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/74099824-bee?shelf=reread-many-times">reread-many-times</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/74099824-bee?shelf=alpha-male-hero">alpha-male-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/74099824-bee?shelf=favorite-hero">favorite-hero</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3332617565" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4155678113862111426"><i>5 STARS</i><br/><br/>This.<br/>Was.<br/>So.<br/>Good.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1589301998ra/29463080.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I've been having to read about annoying heroes that felt like <i>boys</i> for a while now. I was craving something or someone super possessive, maybe a little crazy. A lot dysfunctional and perhaps teeny tiny bit over the top. I was craving a good ol' fashioned man. And boy did Knight deliver.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>“I’ll kill him, he touches you again,” he murmured.<br/>Oh boy.<br/>“Knight,” I breathed, my fingers clenching tighter in his tee.<br/>“Kill anyone, they touch you."</b>
</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509671513ra/24347051.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Knight was every inch of a man. At </span>
  <span id="freeText4155678113862111426" style="display:none"><i>5 STARS</i><br><br>This.<br>Was.<br>So.<br>Good.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1589301998ra/29463080.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I've been having to read about annoying heroes that felt like <i>boys</i> for a while now. I was craving something or someone super possessive, maybe a little crazy. A lot dysfunctional and perhaps teeny tiny bit over the top. I was craving a good ol' fashioned man. And boy did Knight deliver.<br><br><i>
  <b>“I’ll kill him, he touches you again,” he murmured.<br>Oh boy.<br>“Knight,” I breathed, my fingers clenching tighter in his tee.<br>“Kill anyone, they touch you."</b>
</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509671513ra/24347051.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Knight was every inch of a man. At times I had to take some breaks because he didn't pull ANY punches with Anya - or anyone else for that matter - and I'd get annoyed with how OTT he was, but at the same time my stomach was clenching and I was blushing and giggling and just plainly falling in love with his overbearing ass. He was perhaps the most alpha-ish hero I've read about to date (and that's saying something...). And when I tell you he was alpha, I mean it. He would tell Anya what to do, what to dress, would get mad at her if she didn't comply.<br><br>And. The. Heroine. Loved. It.<br><br><i>
  <b>Call me crazy, but I was the woman for him just as I was, and just as he was, Knight Sebring was the man for me.</b>
</i><br><br>Often times authors claim that they are pairing their characters with people they're supposed to be with *eye roll*. People that I personally feel like don't understand them, reject them or fight them every step of the way, so much so I start to struggle to feel the couple's love or connection. In Knight and Anya's case? It was the exact opposite. These two really did belong together. She understood him, he understood her, <i>they understood each other.</i> They both had boundaries that the other would respect and understand. And if Anya, or me, or you, or ANYONE, likes their men to be crazy possessive, who are we to judge? Because, in Tabitha Brown's words: <i>that's yo business.</i><br><br><i>
  <b>I knew then I was giving him everything, just the same as he was giving me. And that meant everything to me.</b>
</i><br><br>Anya was such an awesome heroine. I really liked her and enjoyed being inside her head. There were times I wanted her to maybe fight Knight a little more, but like I said, that's her business.<br><br>The romance was steamy hot, a little Crazy with a capital C, but also so darn sweet. There were definitely butterflies in my belly while I read their scenes together. No OP drama, no miscommunication. Just a good old love story with a lot of craziness on the side. Exactly what I was in the mood for.<br><br><i>
  <b>“You can’t cushion me from the entire world, Knight.”<br>“I can try.”</b>
</i><br><br>I loved this book. Loved, loved it. I gotta warn you though. There is some daddy play involved in the sex. NOT full-on daddy kink, and I'd say it's from the light end of the spectrum (?). Personally, it's not something that I enjoy per se, but in this book I didn't mind it at all (and found it hot).<br><br>This book definitely comes highly recommended if you're in the mood for a crazy ass hero and some hot lovin'!<br><br><i>
  <b>“You love me?”<br>“Baby, you were made for me.”</b>
</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4155678113862111426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('p4VA7Fw1iKt2RuIkmIYkXWNHUDFtLdj+RSIuaPIf3lUw7MmHKF0Yc8pfPt5UWiaEYFNePajVdCbwUq2KmLEuJw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rOKQEU51XhmfM2pMP1Ph8+dfF/SjUsFtJdddLoVB1yo7ixl6Oh3OwSMqtrbzj+Mq5EsZ+GaqbbWQp97M7+8nWA==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText8831540355973766326" style="display:none">Kristen Ashley was born in Gary, Indiana, USA. She nearly killed her mother and herself making it into the world, seeing as she had the umbilical cord wrapped around her neck (already attempting to accessorise and she hadn't taken her first breath!). <br /><br />Kristen grew up in Brownsburg, Indiana but has lived in Denver, Colorado and the West Country of England. Thus she has been blessed to have friends and family around the globe. Her posse is loopy (to say the least) but loopy is good when you want to write.<br /><br />Kristen was raised in a house with a large and multi-generational family. They lived on a very small farm in a small town in the heartland and existed amongst the strains of Glenn Miller, The Everly Brothers, REO Speedwagon and Whitesnake (and the wardrobes that matched).<br /><br />Needless to say, growing up in a house full of music, clothes and love was a good way to grow up. <br /><br />And as she keeps growing up, it keeps getting better.</span>
